                        cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-Assembled Fe3O4 Nanoparticle Clusters as High-Performance Anodes for Lithium Ion Batteries via Geometric Confinement</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee, Soo Hong; Yu, Seung-Ho; Lee, Ji Eun; Jin, Aihua; Lee, Dong Jun; Lee, Nohyun; Jo, Hyungyung; Shin, Kwangsoo; Ahn, Tae-Young; Kim, Young-Woon; Choe, Heeman; Sung, Yung-Eun; Hyeon, Taeghwan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4249-4256</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Although different kinds of metal oxide nanoparticles continue to be proposed as anode materials for lithium-ion batteries, their cycle life and power d. are still not suitable for com. applications.  Metal oxide nanoparticles have a large storage capacity, but they suffer from the excessive generation of solid-electrolyte interphase on the surface, low elec. cond., and mech. degrdn. and pulverization resulted from severe vol. expansion during cycling.  Herein we present the prepn. of mesoporous iron oxide nanoparticle clusters by a bottom-up self-assembly approach and demonstrate that they exhibit excellent cyclic stability and rate capability derived from their three-dimensional mesoporous nanostructure.  By controlling the geometric configuration, we can achieve stable interfaces between the electrolyte and active materials, resulting in solid-electrolyte interphase formation confined on the outer surface of the mesoporous iron oxide nanoparticle clusters.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq-15JkZmTfF7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liCk3wiOlRoZw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtF2rurbO&amp;md5=1d05719c6dd41817fa6b84f5bc7aa0ac</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201502938"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Smart hybrids of Zn<sub>2</sub>GeO<sub>4</sub> nanoparticles and ultrathin g-C<sub>3</sub>N<sub>4</sub> layers: synergistic lithium storage and excellent electrochemical performance</span>. <i>Adv. Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>25</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">44</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">6858</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">6866</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.201502938</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D25%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D6858-6866%26journal%3DAdv.%2BFunct.%2BMater.%26issue%3D44%26author%3DX.%2BLi%26author%3DY.%2BFeng%26author%3DM.%2BLi%26author%3DW.%2BLi%26author%3DH.%2BWei%26author%3DD.%2BSong%26title%3DSmart%2Bhybrids%2Bof%2BZn2GeO4%2Bnanoparticles%2Band%2Bultrathin%2Bg-C3N4%2Blayers%253A%2Bsynergistic%2Blithium%2Bstorage%2Band%2Bexcellent%2Belectrochemical%2Bperformance%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadfm.201502938&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c09246&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadfm.201502938&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Smart Hybrids of Zn2GeO4 Nanoparticles and Ultrathin g-C3N4 Layers: Synergistic Lithium Storage and Excellent Electrochemical Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Xiaodan; Feng, Yi; Li, Meicheng; Li, Wei; Wei, Hao; Song, Dandan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">44</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6858-6866</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Smart hybrids of Zn2GeO4 nanoparticles and ultrathin g-C3N4 layers (Zn2GeO4/g-C3N4 hybrids) are realized by a facile soln. approach, where g-C3N4 layers act as an effective substrate for the nucleation and subsequent in situ growth of Zn2GeO4 nanoparticles.  A synergistic effect is demonstrated on the two building blocks of Zn2GeO4/g-C3N4 hybrids for lithium storage: Zn2GeO4 nanoparticles contribute high capacity and serve as spacers to isolate the ultrathin g-C3N4 layers from restacking, resulting in expanded interlayer and exposed vacancies with doubly bonded nitrogen for extra Li-ion storage and diffusion pathway, 2D g-C3N4 layers, in turn, minimize the strain of particles expansion and prevent the formation of unstable solid electrolyte interphase, leading to highly reversible lithium storage.  Benefiting from the remarkable synergy, the Zn2GeO4/g-C3N4 hybrids exhibit highly reversible capacity of 1370 mA h/g at 200 mA/g after 140 cycles and excellent rate capability of 950 mA h/g at 2000 mA/g.  The synergistic effect originating from the hybrids brings out excellent electrochem. performance, and thus casts new light on the development of high-energy and high-power anode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpuNTu_9wOL5bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liCk3wiOlRoZw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1Gkt7%252FE&amp;md5=afaafa93e477279360b9482ceb2794e5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref4"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref4'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">4</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit4" data-doi="10.1016/j.jhazmat.2018.03.003"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Construction of multifunctional MoSe2 hybrid towards the simultaneous improvements in fire safety and mechanical property of polymer</span>. <i>J. Strong interfacial interactions between the functionalized MoSe2 sheets and TPU can be obtained, making more efficient load transfer from the weak polymer chains to the robust sheets.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon coated mixed-metal selenide microrod: Bimetal-organic-framework derivation approach and applications for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sun, Weiwei; Cai, Chang; Tang, Xuxu; Lv, Li-Ping; Wang, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transitional metal selenides can be explored as a class of candidate electrodes for lithium-ion batteries, because of their large lithium storage ability, wide availability, and good safety.  Besides, hybridization with carbonaceous materials, as well as the design of porous or hollow structure, would be effective approaches to improve the cycling stability and rate performance of transitional metal selenide electrodes.  By a facile bimetal-org.-framework approach, a carbon-coated bimetal selenide microrod composite (Co-Zn-Se@C) is fabricated for the first time in this work.  On account of the MOF-derived porous particle-assembled structure, along with the buffering effect between two metal components, the Co-Zn-Se@C electrode manifests extremely large reversible capacity of 949 mAh/g after 500 cycles with good high-rate capability for lithium ion batteries.                         cas_cit9R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">9</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Building Fast Diffusion Channel by Constructing Metal Sulfide/Metal Selenide Heterostructures for High-Performance Sodium Ion Batteries Anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Tianshuai; Legut, Dominik; Fan, Yanchen; Qin, Jian; Li, Xifei; Zhang, Qianfan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">20</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6199-6205</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Heterostructure engineering is one of the most promising modification strategies toward improving sluggish kinetics for the anode of sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, we report a systemic investigation on the different types of heterostructure interfaces' effects of discharging products (Na2O, Na2S, Na2Se) on the rate performance.  First-principle calcns. reveal that the Na2S/Na2Se interface possesses the lowest diffusion energy barrier (0.39 eV) of Na among three kinds of interface structures (Na2O/Na2S, Na2O/Na2Se, and Na2S/Na2Se) due to its smallest recorded interface deformation, similar electronegativity, and lattice const.  The exptl. evidence confirms that the metal sulfide/metal selenide (SnS/SnSe2) hierarchical anode exhibits outstanding rate performance, where the normalized capacity at 10 A g-1 compared to 0.1 A g-1 is 45.6%.  The proposed design strategy in this work is helpful to design high rate performance anodes for advanced battery systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo9lxbr-vNIRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhbL2xilIHvew"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhsVKnurzK&amp;md5=1fbe540df7115a96b9529bc9bf10a56e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref10"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">10</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit10" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201802745"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ali, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Asif, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchically porous Fe<sub>2</sub>CoSe<sub>4</sub> binary-metal selenide for extraordinary rate performance and durable anode of sodium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">NiSb/nitrogen-doped carbon derived from Ni-based framework as advanced anode for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Su, Mingru; Li, Jinlin; He, Kuidong; Fu, Kai; Nui, Penghu; Chen, Yichang; Zhou, Yu; Dou, Aichun; Hou, Xiaochuan; Liu, Yunjian</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Colloid and Interface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2023</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">629</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">Part_A</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">83-91</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCISA5</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0021-9797</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Antimony anode has attracted much attention owing to its low lithium-embedded platform and high specific capacity.  However, the dramatic vol. expansion during the insertion and detachment of Li+ seriously affects its application in lithium-ion batteries.  In this work, NiSb alloy embedded in nitrogen-doped carbon (NiSb/C) derived from a Ni-based framework was synthesized by a simple hydrothermal reaction followed by annealing treatment.  NiSb alloy nanoparticles could alleviate significant vol. expansion during lithium/delithiation owing to the good buffering action of Ni.  Nitrogen-doped carbon provides abundant active sites for Li+ and serves as a conductive network to accelerate electron transport.  Moreover, the uniformly dispersed NiSb alloy particles and the nitrogen-doped carbon can effectively cooperate to retain the structural completeness of antimony, which promotes the cycling stability and high-rate performance of the NiSb/C anode.  At a high d. of 2 A g-1, the prepd. NiSb/C anode exhibits a reversible specific capacity of 426 mAh g-1 after 450 cycles.  It can also exhibit a superior rate capability of 387 mAh g-1 at 5.0 A g-1, which can provide a possibility for designing new anode materials for rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoR2xfqn9g7mrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj-wHNR5BUsZA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38Xit1ylsLjF&amp;md5=aba142295a86500d8c82d636af0dc462</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.3c02865"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shan, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oli, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Florez Gomez, J.                 10.1038/ncomms6261</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3D5261%26journal%3DNat.%2BCommun.%26issue%3D1%26author%3DF.%2BZheng%26author%3DY.%2BYang%26author%3DQ.%2BChen%26title%3DHigh%2Blithium%2Banodic%2Bperformance%2Bof%2Bhighly%2Bnitrogen-doped%2Bporous%2Bcarbon%2Bprepared%2Bfrom%2Ba%2Bmetal-organic%2Bframework%26doi%3D10.1038%252Fncomms6261&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c09246&amp;doiOfLink=10.1038%2Fncomms6261&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High lithium anodic performance of highly nitrogen-doped porous carbon prepared from a metal-organic framework</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zheng, Fangcai; Yang, Yang; Chen, Qianwang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5261</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-1723</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Theor. and exptl. results have revealed that the lithium-ion storage capacity for nitrogen-doped graphene largely depends on the nitrogen-doping level.  However, most nitrogen-doped carbon materials used for lithium-ion batteries are reported to have a nitrogen content of approx. 10 wt% because a higher no. of nitrogen atoms in the two-dimensional honeycomb lattice can result in structural instability.  Here we report nitrogen-doped graphene particle analogs with a nitrogen content of up to 17.72 wt% that are prepd. by the pyrolysis of a nitrogen-contg. zeolitic imidazolate framework at 800 °C under a nitrogen atm.  As an anode material for lithium-ion batteries, these particles retain a capacity of 2,132 mA h g-1 after 50 cycles at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1, and 785 mAh g-1 after 1,000 cycles at 5 A g-1.  The remarkable performance results from the graphene analogous particles doped with nitrogen within the hexagonal lattice and edges.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDx-A-uZG9bbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj-wHNR5BUsZA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFeisLvE&amp;md5=54792435037037c3dbd58dd2ece8d10e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202110048"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qi, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jensen, L.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Metal-Organic Framework Glass Anode with an Exceptional Cycling-Induced Capacity Enhancement for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gao, Chengwei; Jiang, Zhenjing; Qi, Shibin; Wang, Peixing; Jensen, Lars Rosgaard; Johansen, Morten; Christensen, Christian Kolle; Zhang, Yanfei; Ravnsbaek, Dorthe Bomholdt; Yue, Yuanzheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Metal-org. frameworks (MOFs) hold great promise as high-energy anode materials for next-generation lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) due to their tunable chem., pore structure and abundant reaction sites.  However, the pore structure of cryst. MOFs tends to collapse during lithium-ion insertion and extn., and hence, their electrochem. performances are rather limited.  As a crit. breakthrough, a MOF glass anode for LIBs has been developed in the present work.  In detail, it is fabricated by melt-quenching Cobalt-ZIF-62 (Co(Im)1.75(bIm)0.25) to glass, and then by combining glass with carbon black and binder.  The derived anode exhibits high lithium storage capacity (306 mAh g-1 after 1000 cycles at of 2 A g-1), outstanding cycling stability, and superior rate performance compared with the cryst. Cobalt-ZIF-62 and the amorphous one prepd. by high-energy ball-milling.  Importantly, it is found that the Li-ion storage capacity of the MOF glass anode continuously rises with charge-discharge cycling and even tripled after 1000 cycles.  Combined spectroscopic and structural analyses, along with d. functional theory calcns., reveal the origin of the cycling-induced enhancement of the performances of the MOF glass anode, i.e., the increased distortion and local breakage of the CoN coordination bonds making the Li-ion intercalation sites more accessible.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq3Dh0-ia9SxbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgzZtHLKaYktQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XisFKht74%253D&amp;md5=37155cf46c994429f9831ba34edaea7c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202301109"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fundamental Understanding and Facing Challenges in Structural Design of Porous Si-Based Anodes for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Fundamental Understanding and Facing Challenges in Structural Design of Porous Si-Based Anodes for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Zhongling; Jiang, Hao; Zhang, Xinlin; Cheng, Fangyi; Wu, Minghong; Zhang, Haijiao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  As one of the most electrochem. energy storage devices, lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) remain the workhorse of the energy market due to their unparalleled advantages.  Remarkably, Si-based materials play a pivotal role in LIBs anodes owing to ultrahigh theor. capacity of Si and rich natural resources.  However, bulk silicon materials are difficult to meet the current com. demand because of their low cond., sluggish reaction kinetics, and huge vol. expansion.  The construction of porous structures has been acknowledged as an effective way to solve the above issues.  Herein, the delicate design of porous Si-based anode materials including synthetic strategies, the engineering of surface morphol. and micro/nano-structure, and the regulation of different compns., as well as their applications in LIBs is systematically summarized.  Particularly, the fine engineering of different pore parameters for Si-based materials is on focus.  Importantly, the relationship between thick electrodes and tortuosity/porosity, and the structural effect between pores and battery performance are also discussed in depth.  Finally, the applications of porous Si-based anodes in full-cells and their com. achievements are briefly described.  This review is expected to provide a basic understanding and deep insight into developing porous Si-based anodes for high-energy lithium storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRdzUXRg5lRrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgzZtHLKaYktQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ growth-optimized synthesize of Al-MOF@RGO anode materials with long-life capacity-enhanced lithium-ion storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Kai; Chen, Jiangchun; Hou, Fengxiao; Wang, Han; Zhang, Yaohui; Zhong, Xiaobin; Song, Yuexian; Zhang, Yangang; Zhang, Zhiwen; Liu, Hantao; Liang, Junfei; Wang, Hua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Low lithium ions transport capacity, poor electronic cond., and the structural stability of metal org. frameworks (MOFs) severely restrict the development of practical lithium-ion batteries (LIBs).  Therefore, many researchers were motivated to conduct investigations from the direction of both pore size regulation and composite synthesize for MOF-based materials.  In the present work, the Al-MOF (Al(OH)[O2C-C6H4-CO2]) particles with well-developed pore structures were conceived.  They were optimized by adjusting the hydrothermal self-assembly reaction time and temp., particularly when the pore size increased from micropores to mesopores, which greatly improves the transport capacity of lithium ions.  Then, the in-situ growth-optimized Al-MOF particles on the reduced graphene oxide (RGO) layer can effectively improve electronic cond. and structural stability through the dual regulation of electrostatic attraction and heterogeneous nucleation.  The RGO-supported Al-MOF@RGO anode used in LIBs exhibits a specific capacity of 468.5 mAh/g after 1000 cycles at a c.d. of 1.0 A/g.  The specific capacity of the Al-MOF@RGO anode is still as high as 282.0 mAh/g after 1000 cycles even at 2.0 A/g.  As expected, the in-situ growth-optimized synthesize of the Al-MOF@RGO anode with a long-life capacity-enhanced trend shows superior lithium storage performance.  The Al-MOF@RGO//LiFePO4 full cell measurement demonstrates its potential of com. applications in LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrWUt2AEPMJDLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgzZtHLKaYktQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XivFOjsrbM&amp;md5=216ff78e19d2390256aacd3e20d3b21a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b01430"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Carreon, M.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Optimized assembling of MOF/SnO2/Graphene leads to superior anode for lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gao, Chengwei; Jiang, Zhenjing; Wang, Peixing; Jensen, Lars Rosgaard; Zhang, Yanfei; Yue, Yuanzheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">74</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">104868</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">SnO2 is one of the most promising anode materials for lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  However, its cycling stability is poor due to its large vol. change, and hence, its practical applications in LIBs are hindered.  In this work, we propose a novel and simple strategy to enhance the performances of SnO2-based anodes.  This strategy involves optimized assembling of SnO2 with metal org. framework (MOF) and graphene.  SnO2 nanoparticles are packed into Al-MOF in an optimum mass ratio, and then the derived SnO2@MOF composite is wrapped by graphene, finally resulting in the SnO2@MOF/graphene composite.  This composite exhibits greatly enhanced cycling stability, i.e., the specific capacity is about 450 mA h g-1 after 1000 charge/discharge cycles at the c.d. of 1000 mA g-1.  This is attributed to the unique structural configuration of the composite, which gives rich accessible electroactive sites, shortened ion transport pathways, and superior electronic cond.  The MOF protection layer is a key for improving the lithium storage of metal oxide-based anodes.  Although the capacity of the SnO2@MOF/graphene composite is not the highest among the existing anode materials, its synthesis process is simpler and cost effective.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqKVDEvZPq1GLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhSqd89r2kpbw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXpsl2htbg%253D&amp;md5=1f1f701ee045641f390cc579469529a8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.3c04341"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dai, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fang, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chu, P.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Comparison analysis on the thermal runaway of lithium-ion battery under two heating modes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Tangqin; Chen, Haodong; Wang, Qingsong; Sun, Jinhua</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Hazardous Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">344</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">733-741</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JHMAD9</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0304-3894</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The thermal stability evaluation of materials in a soft-pack com. cell is tested using C80 calorimeter, including anode, cathode, separator and full cell (mixing of the three materials including addnl. electrolyte).  Thermal runaway characteristic of the com. cell is tested on the accelerating rate calorimeter (ARC) with 2 heating modes, including internal heating mode and external heating mode.  The results show that the thermal stability of internal material for tested cell is: anode &lt; separator &lt; cathode.  The voltage drop is influenced by the consumption of cathode and separator, while the effect of anode consumption on the voltage can be negligible.  Both onset temp. and crit. temp. in external heating mode are larger than that in internal heating mode.  Thermal runaway induced by high temp. of the tested cell can be divided into 3 stages: (1) the cell can work under normal mode and all the internal exothermal reaction can be ignorable, (2) the exothermal of anode which can be detected and the thermal runaway can be stopped by effective heat dissipation, and (3) the cathode reaction and separator melting which cause the cell voltage drop and thermal runaway of the cell is inevitable in this stage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo6J8mrngtxBLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhSqd89r2kpbw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhvVajsbbL&amp;md5=7218e4bc933ccd73dcb410ddf3db2851</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1016/j.jhazmat.2020.123169"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Identification and characteristic analysis of powder ejected from a lithium ion battery during thermal runaway at elevated temperatures</span>. <i>J. Power Sources</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2021</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>498</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">229908</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2021.229908</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D498%26publication_year%3D2021%26pages%3D229908%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DB.%2BHuang%26author%3DH.%2BHua%26author%3DL.%2BPeng%26author%3DX.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BShen%26author%3DR.%2BLi%26author%3DP.%2BZhang%26author%3DJ.%2BZhao%26title%3DThe%2Bfunctional%2Bseparator%2Bfor%2Blithium-ion%2Bbatteries%2Bbased%2Bon%2Bphosphonate%2Bmodified%2Bnano-scale%2Bsilica%2Bceramic%2Bparticles%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2021.229908&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c09246&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2021.229908&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The functional separator for lithium-ion batteries based on phosphonate modified nano-scale silica ceramic particles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Boyang; Hua, Haiming; Peng, Longqing; Wang, Xin; Shen, Xiu; Li, Ruiyang; Zhang, Peng; Zhao, Jinbao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">498</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">229908</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), benefiting from various functional components, functional separators can possess different capabilities to cope with the risks in complex application scenarios.  In this work, a functional separator based on the phosphonate-modified nano-scale silica ceramic particles is fabricated to reduce the safety risks in LIBs.  Through an anhyd. polymn. process, di-Me vinylphosphonate (DMVP), a kind of widely used flame retardants, is grafted on silica (SiO2).  Then the modified SiO2 (mSiO2) is coated on the pristine polyethylene separator by a typical coating process.  Combining the function of the ceramic and phosphonate, the modified ceramic separator displays substantially enhanced thermal stability, without visual thermal shrink up to 200°C.  The flame resistances of separator itself and pouch cells are also significantly improved, even though flammable electrolyte is added.  Different from the case when the phosphonate is used as an additive in electrolyte, the phosphonate is fixed firmly on the separator and not easy to be embedded in carbon anode after battery cycles.  The coin cells assembled with the modified separators are away from the irreversible loss of discharge capacity and low Coulombic efficiency for the first cycle, which can be attributed to the firm immobilization of org. phosphonate.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPItbnZAK6v7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4IS0c4BjA_g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXpsVSqtro%253D&amp;md5=50c1664b4ff29308780585bc6f7cb59c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1016/j.jhazmat.2018.09.009"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Construction of multifunctional boron nitride nanosheet towards reducing toxic volatiles (CO and HCN) generation and fire hazard of thermoplastic polyurethane</span>. <i>J. Hazard. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>362</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">482</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">494</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jhazmat.2018.09.009</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D362%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D482-494%26journal%3DJ.%2BHazard.%2BMater.%26author%3DJ.%2BWang%26author%3DD.%2BZhang%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DW.%2BCai%26author%3DC.%2BYao%26author%3DY.%2BHu%26author%3DW.%2BHu%26title%3DConstruction%2Bof%2Bmultifunctional%2Bboron%2Bnitride%2Bnanosheet%2Btowards%2Breducing%2Btoxic%2Bvolatiles%2B%2528CO%2Band%2BHCN%2529%2Bgeneration%2Band%2Bfire%2Bhazard%2Bof%2Bthermoplastic%2Bpolyurethane%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jhazmat.2018.09.009&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c09246&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jhazmat.2018.09.009&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Construction of multifunctional boron nitride nanosheet towards reducing toxic volatiles (CO and HCN) generation and fire hazard of thermoplastic polyurethane</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Junling; Zhang, Dichang; Zhang, Yan; Cai, Wei; Yao, Congxue; Hu, Yuan; Hu, Weizhao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Hazardous Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">362</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">482-494</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JHMAD9</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0304-3894</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Considerable toxic volatiles (CO and HCN) generation and high fire hazard has definitely compromised the application of thermoplastic polyurethane (TPU).  Here, a novel functionalization strategy for bulky h-BN is adopted to obtain the multifunctional CPBN, aiming at the flame retardancy reinforcement of TPU.  The multifunctional CPBN is successfully prepd. via the wrapping of phytic acid doped polypyrrole shell, following with the adsorption of copper ions.  The obviously decreased peak heat release rate, peak smoke prodn. rate and total smoke prodn. values, obtained from cone test, confirms the reduced fire hazard of TPU composite with CPBN.  The dramatic suppressions on CO and HCN releases can also be obsd. from TG-IR test.  Tensile test demonstrates that adding CPBN favors the reinforcement in mech. property of TPU.  Thus, the concurrent improvements in flame retardancy and mech. performance are achieved by incorporating CPBN.  This work opens up new avenues for the functionalization of h-BN, and thus facilitates its promising applications in polymer-matrix composite.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqVNYFDE4_VrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4IS0c4BjA_g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXhvVKmt7%252FM&amp;md5=7e2baaab1cd9b492539cb3b170b5b234</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2021.129087"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kan, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Construction of multifunctional and flame retardant separator towards stable lithium-sulfur batteries with high safety</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Construction of multifunctional and flame retardant separator towards stable lithium-sulfur batteries with high safety</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Junling; Cai, Wei; Mu, Xiaowei; Han, Longfei; Wu, Na; Liao, Can; Kan, Yongchun; Hu, Yuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2021</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">416</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">129087</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Considering the unprecedented advantages such as superb theor. capacity, high energy d. and low cost, lithium-sulfur batteries (LSBs) have been under spotlight in past several years.  Nevertheless, limited by its intrinsic drawbacks of highly insulating character, serious shuttle effect and lithium dendrites growth, there is still a long way from large-scale application of LSBs.  Here, a polyacrylonitrile@metal org. frameworks (PAN@MOFs) composite-derived heteroatoms doped carbon@encapsulated CoS2 nanoparticles (NSPCFS@CoS2) modified separator is designed to surmount these issues.  Notably, the modified separator shows improved flame retardancy.  By using this separator, the effective suppression on shuttle behavior as well as boost in polysulfides conversion kinetics are realized, which can be assigned to the integrative superiorities of conductive carbon fiber network, electrocatalytic activity, polar-polar interaction and Lewis acid-base interaction.  The cell with modified separator shows an initial discharge capacity of 1140.7 mAh g-1.  After running for 100 cycles, a high capacity of 631.6 mAh g-1 is retained.  Notably, the inhibited growth of lithium dendrites is also obtained, indicating the promoted battery safety.  Overall, this work may provide useful inspirations for the utilization of MOFs-derived hierarchical composite in implementing safer high-performance LSBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp9soHFKvNq9rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4IS0c4BjA_g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3MXltlyls70%253D&amp;md5=5d98a189cf5357c4caae5839f3d69d40</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcis.2023.02.011"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bai, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Designing of trimetallic-phase ternary metal sulfides coupled with N/S doped carbon protector for superior and safe Li/Na storage</span>. <i>J.                 10.1016/0368-2048(86)80043-3</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D40%26publication_year%3D1986%26pages%3D329-337%26journal%3DJ.%2BElectron%2BSpectrosc.%2BRelat.%2BPhenom.%26issue%3D4%26author%3DM.%2BShenasa%26author%3DS.%2BSainkar%26author%3DD.%2BLichtman%26title%3DXPS%2Bstudy%2Bof%2Bsome%2Bselected%2Bselenium%2Bcompounds%26doi%3D10.1016%252F0368-2048%252886%252980043-3&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c09246&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2F0368-2048%2886%2980043-3&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">XPS study of some selected selenium compounds</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shenasa, Mohsen; Sainkar, Sudhakar; Lichtman, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Electron Spectroscopy and Related Phenomena</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">40</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">XPS of the Se 3d peak in Se, SeO2, As2Se3, ZnSe, CdSe, CoSe, FeSe, CrSe, VSe2, and TiSe were studied.  In the case of As2Se3, ZnSe, CdSe, CoSe, and CrSe, as the change in electronegativity of the anion increased, the change in the binding energy value of the Se 3d peak increased.  In all of the Se compds. studied, the Se-Se bond in pure Se is stronger than the Se-X bond, where X = As, Zn, Cd, Co, Fe, Cr, V, and Ti.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp5uiDtlYdVXbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg4IS0c4BjA_g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaL28XlvVSru7c%253D&amp;md5=6368e8a6292cea762ae1d23ba0508a71</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1016/0169-4332(95)00079-8"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jackson, S. T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nuzzo, R. G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Determining hybridization differences for amorphous carbon from the XPS C 1s envelope</span>. <i>Appl. Surf. Sci.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1995</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>90</i></span> (<span class="NLM_issue">2</span>),  <span class="NLM_fpage">195</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">203</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/0169-4332(95)00079-8</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D90%26publication_year%3D1995%26pages%3D195-203%26journal%3DAppl.%2BSurf.%2BSci.%26issue%3D2%26author%3DS.%2BT.%2BJackson%26author%3DR.%2BG.%2BNuzzo%26title%3DDetermining%2Bhybridization%2Bdifferences%2Bfor%2Bamorphous%2Bcarbon%2Bfrom%2Bthe%2BXPS%2BC%2B1s%2Benvelope%26doi%3D10.1016%252F0169-4332%252895%252900079-8&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c09246&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2F0169-4332%2895%2900079-8&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Determining hybridization differences for amorphous carbon from the XPS C 1s envelope</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jackson, Stuart T.; Nuzzo, Ralph G.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Applied Surface Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1995</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">90</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">195-203</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ASUSEE</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0169-4332</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two kinds of amorphous carbon (a-C) thin film samples were synthesized, one by magnetron sputtering, the other by filtered cathodic arc deposition.  XPS showed that the C 1s envelope for each sample was primarily a convolution of three peaks which are assignable to sp2 hybridized carbon, sp3 hybridized carbon (shifted from the sp2 peak by ∼1 eV), and an sp2 satellite peak, possibly due to π-π* transition.  The satellite typically comprised just under 14% of the total sp2 signal and was shifted from the main sp2 peak by ∼2 eV.  The relative amts. of each bonding type were detd. by comparing the integrated areas of the sp2 and sp3 peaks.  Auger electron spectroscopy (AES) was also performed on these samples, along with highly ordered pyrolytic graphite (100% sp2) and natural diamond (100% sp3) for comparison purposes.  The binding energy width D between the highest max. and lowest min. values of the first deriv. C (KLL) spectra were obtained, and a linear relationship between D and the amt. of sp3 bonding assumed.  When comparing sp3 values obtained by AES and deconvoluted XPS spectra an error range within ±1.5% was found, making XPS a satisfactory method for obtaining hybridization information.  It was noted that Ar+ ion bombardment has a substantial effect on the surface sp2/sp3 ratio, as obsd. by XPS.  These results are related to other studies of ion bombardment of graphite and diamond.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoDHDwxMtY2VbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh8xwIjmKsM2A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK2MXotValsb4%253D&amp;md5=51e3fda6d2be41dea3fb761d8c291023</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref44"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">44</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit44" data-doi="10.1016/S0368-2048(02)00284-0"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Leiro, J. H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Laiho, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Batirev, I.                 10.1016/j.cej.2021.134328</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D432%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D134328%26journal%3DChem.%2BEng.%2BJ.%26author%3DJ.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BWei%26author%3DZ.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BHe%26author%3DC.%2BWang%26author%3DH.%2BLin%26author%3DY.%2BDeng%26title%3DMOFs-derived%2Bself-sacrificing%2Btemplate%2Bstrategy%2Bto%2Bdouble-shelled%2Bmetal%2Boxides%2Bnanocages%2Bas%2Bhierarchical%2Binterfacial%2Bcatalyst%2Bfor%2Bsuppressing%2Bsmoke%2Band%2Btoxic%2Bgases%2Breleases%2Bof%2Bepoxy%2Bresin%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.cej.2021.134328&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c09246&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.cej.2021.134328&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MOFs-derived self-sacrificing template strategy to double-shelled metal oxides nanocages as hierarchical interfacial catalyst for suppressing smoke and toxic gases releases of epoxy resin</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Junling; Wei, Yanan; Wang, Zhirong; He, Xinrui; Wang, Chao; Lin, Hu; Deng, Yingxuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">432</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">134328</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMEJAJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1385-8947</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The emission of considerable smoke and toxic gases has been the notorious stumbling block on the extended usage of epoxy resin (EP), which often causes serious fire casualties in real fire.  Hence, metal org. frameworks (MOFs)-derived self-sacrificing template strategy is adopted, to prep. metal oxides double-shelled nanocages (Co3O4/Co3O4 and Co3O4/NiCo2O4 DSNCs) as hierarchical interfacial catalysts for suppressing the releases of smoke and toxic gases.  With the addn. of 2.0 wt% Co3O4/Co3O4 DSNCs, the peak smoke prodn. rate (PSPR), total smoke prodn. (TSP), peak CO prodn. rate (PCOP) and total CO prodn. (TCOP) are reduced by 15.8%, 46.9%, 36.2% and 49.1%, sep.  When 2.0 wt% Co3O4/NiCo2O4 DSNCs is incorporated, the PSPR, TSP, PCOP and TCOP are markedly decreased by 40.8%, 55.5%, 46.6% and 48.5%, resp.  These results strongly corroborate the efficacy of DSNCs in suppressing the emission of smoke and toxic CO gas.  Addnl., the values of peak heat release rate are reduced by 15.9% and 28.4%, reflecting the inhibited heat release.  Flame retardancy comparison with reported works corroborates the prominent merit of DSNCs in inhibiting the smoke release.  The clear evidence for suppressed toxic CO and NO gases releases is also acquired from TG-IR test.  Profiting from the well-formed nanoflake-polymer interfaces, the mech. performance is obviously improved.  In short, these designed DSNCs possess great efficacy in smoke as well as toxic gases removal and mech. enhancement of EP.  This investigation may provide useful inspirations for designing MOFs-derived hierarchical interfacial catalysts, towards impairing the fire toxicity of polymer.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqnIsndVFuK6rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh8xwIjmKsM2A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB38XhtVSlug%253D%253D&amp;md5=7ccc5255d858bad7951f4be21d987d84</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcis.2024.02.212"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuen, R.                         cas_cit47R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">47</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Strongly coupled metal-organic frameworks on layered bimetallic hydroxide derived N, S co-doped porous carbon frameworks embedding with CoS2 for energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Junling; Han, Longfei; Wu, Na; Zhang, Zixuan; Liao, Can; Wang, Jingwen; Kan, Yongchun; Hu, Yuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, the fabrication is reported of N, S co-doped carbon framework with confined CoS2 nanoparticles and rooted carbon nanotubes (NSPCF@CoS2).  As LIBs anode, the NSPCF@CoS2 electrode gives an inceptive discharge capacity of 921.5 mA h g-1, with Coulombic efficiency of &gt; 97% during the 200 cycles (except for the previous 5 cycles).  As SIBs anode (the applied voltage range is 0.4-3 V), the NSPCF@CoS2 electrode performs a steady and relatively high capacity (over 448.0 mA h g-1) during the 1650 cycles, and an extremely low capacity decay rate of 0.018% per cycle is obtained.  Also, the NSPCF@CoS2 electrode shows a high capacity of 545.3 mA h g-1 even at 8 A g-1 (the applied voltage range is 0.1-3 V).  This NSPCF@CoS2 electrode shows a comparable or even higher rate performance than many reported transition metal chalcogenides materials, confirming its promising usage.  The presence of pseudocapacitive contribution is verified, after the deep investigation on Li+/Na+ storage behavior and reaction kinetics.  In addn., this rationally designed structure gives potential application in supercapacitor.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp-BFB2E-uvM7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh8xwIjmKsM2A"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXjtVentLk%253D&amp;md5=a4ed4eddb54eabe083b62f8d603d7b38</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref48"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">48</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit48" data-doi="10.1016/j.compositesa.2024.108004"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nie, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yuen, R.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">2 dimensional WS2 tailored nitrogen-doped carbon nanofiber as a highly pseudocapacitive anode material for lithium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Xu; Pei, Chengang; Chen, Wushuang; Feng, Ligang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">To efficiently improve the attractive properties of electrode material for Li ion batteries (LIBs), the uniform hybridization of 2 Dimensional WS2 nanosheets of N doped C nanofiber (WN-CNF) as a novel anode electrode was synthesized via a facile electrospinning strategy. N-contg. groups and 1T phase of WS2 in WN-CNF are demonstrated as the electro-active sites to enhance the capacitive performance.  Meanwhile, WN-CNF exhibits a highly reversible specific capacity of 814mAh g-1 at the c.d. of 100 mAg-1, excellent rate capability of 52% from 100 to 1000 mAg-1 and cyclic stability of 87% after 120 charge/discharge cycles. Bimetallic selenides stand out among multitudinous anode materials on account of their synergistic effects and rich electronic reaction processes.  Here, a nickel-cobalt selenide pompon has been successfully prepd. via a simple solvothermal method.                         cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Thermal runaway features of large format prismatic lithium ion battery using extended volume accelerating rate calorimetry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Feng, Xuning; Fang, Mou; He, Xiangming; Ouyang, Minggao; Lu, Languang; Wang, Hao; Zhang, Mingxuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">255</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">294-301</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The thermal runaway features of a 25 Ah large format prismatic Li ion battery with Li(NixCoyMnz)O2 (NCM) cathode are evaluated using the extended vol.-accelerating rate calorimetry (EV-ARC).  Four thermocouples are set at different positions of the battery.  The temp. inside the battery is 870° or so, much higher than that outside the battery.  The temp. difference is calcd. from the recorded data.  The temp. difference within the battery stays &lt;1° for 97% of the test period, while it rises to its highest, ∼520°, when thermal runaway happens.  The voltage of the battery is also measured during the test.  It takes 15-40 s from the sharp drop of voltage to the instantaneous rise of temp.  Such a time interval is beneficial for early warning of the thermal runaway.  Using a pulse charge/discharge profile, the internal resistance is derived from the quotient of the pulse voltage and the current during the ARC test.  The internal resistance of the battery increases slowly from 20 mΩ to 60 mΩ before thermal runaway, while it rises to 370 mΩ when thermal runaway happens indicating the loss of the integrity of the separator or the battery swell.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrv5xlTB7KCwbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhqRIxPa_Mnig"> &gt;&gt;                 10.1016/j.jallcom.2019.152566</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D816%26publication_year%3D2020%26pages%3D152566%26journal%3DJ.%2BAlloys%2BCompd.%26author%3DW.%2BDing%26author%3DS.%2BWang%26author%3DX.%2BWu%26author%3DY.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DP.%2BZhou%26author%3DT.%2BZhou%26author%3DJ.%2BZhou%26author%3DS.%2BZhuo%26title%3DCo0.85Se%2540C%252FTi3C2Tx%2BMXene%2Bhybrids%2Bas%2Banode%2Bmaterials%2Bfor%2Blithium-ion%2Bbatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jallcom.2019.152566&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.4c09246&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jallcom.2019.152566&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit62R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">62</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Co0.85Se@C/Ti3C2Tx MXene hybrids as anode materials for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ding, Wen; Wang, Shuo; Wu, Xiaozhong; Wang, Yesheng; Li, Yanyan; Zhou, Pengfei; Zhou, Tong; Zhou, Jin; Zhuo, Shuping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">816</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">152566</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JALCEU</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0925-8388</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The volumetric capacity plays a crit. role in lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) on account of the restrictive electrode material.  Herein we report a novel electrode material of Co0.85Se@C/Ti3C2Tx MXene hybrids (CSTCs) with high volumetric capacities are prepd. by ultrasonication of Ti3C2Tx MXene and Co0.85Se@C nanoparticles.  These samples are systematically characterized by X-ray diffraction, scanning and transmission electron microscopy, XPS, and energy dispersive spectroscopy.  The electrochem. performance of these samples as anode materials for LIBs are also studied.  Owing to the opened two-dimensional structure, good electrochem. property, and weak Li+ diffusion resistance, these materials exhibit good electrochem. properties.  The CSTC3 sample delivers the max. reversible capacity, up to 700 mA h g-1 at 0.1 A g-1, corresponding to a very high volumetric capacity of 2044 mA h cm-3 due to its high compact d.  This hybrid is considered to be a promising anode material in small-size wearable or portable electronic devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqW2rrFOiIQ4bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgr8qmjPpZtRg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXhvFOqt73L&amp;md5=25b19500304d072bc46737de88fe17ec</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref63"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref63'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">63</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit63" data-doi="10.1016/j.apsusc.2020.147746"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Miao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhuo, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Three-dimensional graphene-wrapped Co<sub>0.85</sub>Se@C as high volumetric capacity anode material for lithium-ion batteries</span>. <i>Appl.                         cas_cit65R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">65</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sandwich-like Cu2-xSe@C@MoSe2 nanosheets as an improved-performance anode for lithium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jin, Rencheng; Liu, Xiguang; Yang, Lixia; Li, Guihua; Gao, Shanmin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">259</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">841-849</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transition metal chalcogenides are considered as promising materials for Li-ion battery, however, the application in practical devices is still hampered by their poor cycling performance and rate capability.  The authors design and construct sandwich-like Cu2-xSe@C@MoSe2 nanosheets to enhance the cycling and rate performances of Cu2-xSe.  The reversible capacity could be retained at 432 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles at the c.d. of 100 mA g-1.  At 2000 mA g-1, the specific capacity still retains at 163 mAh g-1.  The improved Li storage performance can be attributed to its structural features, which enhance the elec. cond., buffer the vol. change as well as increase their structural stability during cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpPUigVgBDpwbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgr8qmjPpZtRg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhsl2ksL%252FN&amp;md5=585ff1ab6afb846eabdef2a5fc6c0a20</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref66"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref66'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">66</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit66" data-doi="10.1016/j.jcis.2021.01.057"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Stacked Cu<sub>2–x</sub>Se nanoplates with 2D nanochannels as high performance anode for lithium batteries</span>. <i>J.
